#saal ^4kQG4nJZ

strongly connected 
graph ^K4I7iljj

V node v we can 
go to any node w ^CS9mDafl

Dijkstra ^cq9KUdYj

Makes easier to analyze  ^E6wTrEh5

define set T of unexplored neighbours of S ^TYbbLfsD

pick node v e T w. shortest path from S ^Rs4nfQRh

repeat until S=V ^Mp4DrHBk

Finds all shortest path from
source node V node in graph ^tPven7T1

defines a set S
    of iterated nodes  ^dg0iuoLX

update v's distance ^ add to S ^TUBK2nE4

Initial state ^pSFEtbBd

First iteration ^CYuyv7aL

Second iteration  ^UNj2OLDQ

Third iteration  ^ZKNFcgKC

Forth iteration  ^AE0jer1e

proof ^lmagVVzY

induction ^m7XSpo4A

    only have {s}. therefore, we have d(s)=0. optimal path ^1P9aJs47

assume that works on K step. show it works K+1 ^rO89EjPK

goal is to compare P w. Pv and show that P>=Pv ^DgslwV6t

Djikstra (G(V,E), l, s):
 d(s)=0
 Ps=[s]
 S={s}
 while S != V:
     T={w|w e V-S and E v e S s.t. (v, w) e E}
     V w e T,
     let v e T a node of min d'(v)
     let u e S be s.t. d'(v)=d(u)+l(u,v)
     d(v)=d'(v)
     Pv=Pu+[v]
     S=S U {v}
 return d ^ybBOSayE

shortest path to w from nodes e S ^zWEx16Mj
